The Company designs, manufactures, and markets personal computers and related software, services, peripherals, and networking solutions. The Company also designs, develops, and markets line portable digital music players along with related accessories and services including the online distribution third-party music, audio books, music videos, short films, and television shows. The Company\x92 products and services include the Macintosh line desktop and notebook computers, the iPod digital music player, the Xserve server and Xserve RAID storage products, portfolio consumer and professional software applications, the Mac operating system, the iTunes Music Store, portfolio peripherals that support and enhance the Macintosh and iPod product lines, and variety other service and support offerings. The Company sells its products worldwide through its online stores, its own retail stores, its direct sales force, and third-party wholesalers, resellers, and value added resellers. The Company also sells variety third-party products that are compatible with the Company\x92 Macintosh and iPod product lines, including computer printers and printing supplies, storage devices, computer memory, digital camcorders and still cameras, personal digital assistants, iPod accessories, and various other computing products and supplies through its online and retail stores. The Company\x92 fiscal year ends the last Saturday September. Unless otherwise stated, all information presented this Form - based the Company\x92 fiscal calendar. Executive Overview The Company designs, manufactures, and markets personal computers and related software, services, peripherals, and networking solutions. The Company also designs, develops, and markets line portable digital music players along with related accessories and services including the online distribution third-party music, audio books, music videos, short films, and television shows. The Company\x92 products and services include the Macintosh line desktop and notebook computers, the iPod digital music player, the Xserve server and Xserve RAID storage products, portfolio consumer and professional software applications, the Mac operating system, the iTunes Music Store, portfolio peripherals that support and enhance the Macintosh and iPod product lines, and variety other service and support offerings. The Company sells its products worldwide through its online stores, its own retail stores, its direct sales force, and third-party wholesalers, resellers, and value added resellers. addition, the Company sells variety third-party Macintosh compatible products, including computer printers and printing supplies, storage devices, computer memory, digital camcorders and still cameras, personal digital assistants, and various other computing products and supplies through its online and retail stores. The Company sells education, consumer, creative professional, business, and government customers. further description the Company\x92 products may found Part , Item this document under the heading \x93Business.\x94 The Company\x92 business strategy leverages its ability, through the design and development its own operating system, hardware, and many software applications and technologies, bring its customers around the world compelling new products and solutions with superior ease- -use, seamless integration, and innovative industrial design. The Company participates several highly competitive markets, including personal computers with its Macintosh line computers, consumer electronics with its iPod line digital music players, and distribution third-party digital content through its online iTunes Music Store. While the Company widely recognized innovator the personal computer and consumer electronic markets well leader the emerging market for distribution digital content, these are all highly competitive markets that are subject aggressive pricing and increased competition. remain competitive, the Company believes that increased investment research and development ( & ) and marketing and advertising necessary maintain and extend its position the markets where competes. The Company\x92 & spending focused delivering timely updates and enhancements its existing line personal computers, displays, operating systems, software applications, and portable music players; developing new digital lifestyle consumer and professional software applications; and investing new product areas such rack-mount servers, RAID storage systems, and wireless technologies. The Company also believes investment marketing and advertising programs critical increasing product and brand awareness. June , the Company announced its plan begin using Intel microprocessors its Macintosh computers. The Company plans begin shipping certain models with Intel microprocessors June and complete the transition all its Macintosh computers Intel microprocessors the end calendar year . There are potential risks and uncertainties that may occur during this transition, which are further discussed under the heading \x93Factors That May Affect Future Results and Financial Condition.\x94 The Company utilizes variety direct and indirect distribution channels. The Company believes that sales its innovative and differentiated products are enhanced knowledgeable salespersons who can convey the value the hardware, software, and peripheral integration, demonstrate the unique digital lifestyle solutions that are available only Macintosh computers, and demonstrate the compatibility the Macintosh with the Windows platform and networks. The Company further believes that providing SEQ.= ,FOLIO=' ',FILE=' :\\ \\334125947379_D11851_687811\\ - - htm',USER='jmsproofassembler', ='Nov : ' high-quality sales and after-sales support experience critical attracting and retaining customers. ensure high-quality buying experience for its products which service and education are emphasized, the Company has expanded and improved its distribution capabilities opening its own retail stores the . and internationally. The Company had stores open September , . The Company also staffs selected third-party stores with the Company\x92 own employees improve the buying experience through reseller channels. The Company has deployed Apple employees and contractors reseller locations around the world including the ., Europe, Japan, and Australia. The Company also sells customers directly through its online stores around the world. improve access the iPod product line, the Company has significantly expanded the number distribution points where iPods are sold. Critical Accounting Policies and Estimates The preparation financial statements and related disclosures conformity with . generally accepted accounting principles and the Company\x92 discussion and analysis its financial condition and results operations require the Company\x92 management make judgments, assumptions, and estimates that affect the amounts reported its consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes. Note the Notes Consolidated Financial Statements this Form - describes the significant accounting policies and methods used the preparation the Company\x92 consolidated financial statements. Management bases its estimates historical experience and various other assumptions believes reasonable under the circumstances, the results which form the basis for making judgments about the carrying values assets and liabilities. Actual results may differ from these estimates and such differences may material. Management believes the Company\x92 critical accounting policies and estimates are those related revenue recognition, allowance for doubtful accounts, inventory valuation and inventory purchase commitments, warranty costs, and income taxes. Management believes these policies critical because they are both important the portrayal the Company\x92 financial condition and results, and they require management make judgments and estimates about matters that are inherently uncertain. The Company\x92 senior management has reviewed these critical accounting policies and related disclosures with the Audit and Finance Committee the Company\x92 Board Directors. Revenue Recognition Net sales consist primarily revenue from the sale hardware, software, peripherals, digital content, and service and support contracts. The Company recognizes revenue pursuant applicable accounting standards, including Statement Position (SOP) . - , Software Revenue Recognition , amended, and Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) . , Revenue Recognition. The Company recognizes revenue when persuasive evidence arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the sales price fixed determinable, and collection probable. Product considered delivered the customer once has been shipped, and title and risk loss have been transferred. For most the Company\x92 product sales, these criteria are met the time the product shipped. For online sales individuals, for some sales education customers the ., and for certain other sales, the Company defers revenue until the customer receives the product because the Company legally retains portion the risk loss these sales during transit. the outset arrangement the Company determines the arrangement fee not, presumed not , fixed determinable, revenue deferred and subsequently recognized amounts become due and payable. Allowance for Doubtful Accounts The Company distributes its products through third-party resellers and directly certain education, consumer, and commercial customers. The Company generally does not require collateral from its customers. However, when possible the Company does attempt limit credit risk trade receivables with credit insurance for certain customers Latin America, Europe, and Asia and arranging with third-party financing companies provide flooring arrangements and other loan and lease programs the Company\x92 direct customers. These credit-financing arrangements are directly between the third-party financing company and the end customer. such, the Company generally does not assume any recourse credit risk sharing related any these arrangements. However, considerable trade receivables that are not covered collateral, third-party flooring arrangements, credit insurance are outstanding with the Company\x92 distribution and retail channel partners. The allowance for doubtful accounts based management\x92 assessment the collectibility specific customer accounts and includes consideration the credit worthiness and financial condition those specific customers. The Company records allowance reduce the specific receivables the amount that reasonably believed collectible . The Company also records allowance for all other trade receivables based multiple factors including historical experience with bad debts, the general economic environment, the financial condition the Company\x92 distribution channels, and the aging such receivables. there deterioration major customer\x92 financial condition, the Company becomes aware additional information related the credit worthiness major customer, future actual default rates trade receivables general differ from those currently anticipated, the Company may have adjust its allowance for doubtful accounts, which would affect earnings the period the adjustments are made. Factors That May Affect Future Results and Financial Condition Because the following factors, well other factors affecting the Company\x92 operating results and financial condition, past financial performance should not considered reliable indicator future performance, and investors should not use historical trends anticipate results trends future periods. General economic conditions and current economic and political uncertainty could adversely affect the demand for the Company\x92 products and the financial health its suppliers, distributors, and resellers. The Company\x92 operating performance depends significantly general economic conditions the . and abroad. times the past, demand for the Company\x92 products has been negatively impacted difficult global economic conditions. Additionally, some the Company\x92 education customers appeared delaying technology purchases due concerns about the overall impact the weaker economy and state budget deficits their available funding. Although recent macroeconomic trends seem indicate economic recovery, continued uncertainty about future economic conditions makes difficult forecast future demand for the Company\x92 products and related operating results. Quantitative and Qualitative Disclosures About Market Risk Interest Rate and Foreign Currency Risk Management The Company regularly reviews its foreign exchange forward and option positions and its interest rate swap and option positions, both stand-alone basis and conjunction with its underlying foreign currency and interest rate related exposures. However, given the effective horizons the Company\x92 risk management activities and the anticipatory nature the exposures, there can assurance the hedges will offset more than portion the financial impact resulting from movements either foreign exchange interest rates. addition, the timing the accounting for recognition gains and losses related mark- -market instruments for any given period may not coincide with the timing gains and losses related the underlying economic exposures and, therefore, may adversely affect the Company\x92 operating results and financial position. Interest Rate Risk While the Company exposed interest rate fluctuations many the world\x92 leading industrialized countries, the Company\x92 interest income and expense most sensitive fluctuations the general level . interest rates. this regard, changes . interest rates affect the interest earned the Company\x92 cash, cash equivalents, and short-term investments well costs associated with foreign currency hedges. The Company\x92 short-term investment policy and strategy ensure the preservation capital, meet liquidity requirements, and optimize return light the current credit and interest rate environment. The Company benchmarks its performance utilizing external money managers manage small portion the aggregate investment portfolio. The external managers adhere the Company\x92 investment policies and also provide occasional research and market information that supplements internal research used make credit decisions the investment process. The Company\x92 exposure market risk for changes interest rates relates primarily the Company\x92 investment portfolio. The Company places its short-term investments highly liquid securities issued high credit quality issuers and, policy, limits the amount credit exposure any one issuer. The Company\x92 general policy limit the risk principal loss and ensure the safety invested funds limiting market and credit risk. All highly liquid investments with maturities three months less are classified cash equivalents; highly liquid investments with maturities greater than three months are classified short-term investments. September , , approximately $ million the Company\x92 short-term investments had underlying maturities ranging from years. September , , $ million the Company\x92 investment portfolio classified short-term investments had maturities ranging from years. The remainder all had underlying maturities between and months. The Company may sell its investments prior their stated maturities, due liquidity needs, anticipation credit deterioration, for duration management. September , , similar basis point shift the yield curve would have resulted $ million decline fair value. Such losses would only realized the Company sold the investments prior maturity. Except instances noted above, the Company\x92 policy hold investments maturity. Foreign Currency Risk general, the Company net receiver currencies other than the . dollar. Accordingly, changes exchange rates, and particular strengthening the . dollar, may negatively affect the Company\x92 net sales and gross margins expressed . dollars. There also risk that the Company will have adjust local currency product pricing due competitive pressures when there has been significant volatility foreign currency exchange rates. The Company may enter into foreign currency forward and option contracts with financial institutions protect against foreign exchange risks associated with existing assets and liabilities, certain firmly committed transactions, forecasted future cash flows, and net investments foreign subsidiaries. Generally, the Company\x92 practice hedge majority its existing material foreign exchange transaction exposures. However, the Company may not hedge certain foreign exchange transaction exposures due immateriality, prohibitive economic cost hedging particular exposures, and limited availability appropriate hedging instruments. order provide meaningful assessment the foreign currency risk associated with certain the Company\x92 foreign currency derivative positions, the Company performed sensitivity analysis using value- -risk (VAR) model assess the potential impact fluctuations exchange rates. The VAR model consisted using Monte Carlo simulation generate random market price paths. The VAR the maximum expected loss fair value, for given confidence interval, the Company\x92 foreign exchange portfolio due adverse movements rates. The VAR model not intended represent actual losses but used risk estimation and management tool. The model assumes normal market conditions. Forecasted transactions, firm commitments, and assets and liabilities denominated foreign currencies were excluded from the model. Based the results the model, the Company estimates with % confidence maximum one-day loss fair value $ million September , compared maximum one-day loss $ million September , . Because the Company uses foreign currency instruments for hedging purposes, losses incurred those instruments are generally offset increases the fair value the underlying exposures. Actual future gains and losses associated with the Company\x92 investment portfolio and derivative positions may differ materially from the sensitivity analyses performed September , due the inherent limitations associated with predicting the changes the timing and amount interest rates, foreign currency exchanges rates, and the Company\x92 actual exposures and positions. The Company also designs, develops, and markets line portable digital music players along with related accessories and services including the online distribution third-party music, audio books, music videos, short films, and television shows. The Company sells its products worldwide through its online stores, its own retail stores, its direct sales force, and third-party wholesalers, resellers, and value-added resellers. addition its own hardware, software, and peripheral products, the Company sells variety third-party hardware and software products through its online and retail stores. The Company sells education, consumer, creative professional, business, and government customers. Basis Presentation and Preparation The accompanying consolidated financial statements include the accounts the Company. Intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated. The preparation these consolidated financial statements conformity with . generally accepted accounting principles requires management make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported these consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes. Actual results could differ materially from those estimates. Certain prior year amounts the consolidated financial statements and notes thereto have been reclassified conform the current year presentation. The cost securities sold based upon the specific identification method. Foreign Currency Translation The Company translates the assets and liabilities its international non- . functional currency subsidiaries into . dollars using exchange rates effect the end each period. Revenue and expenses for these subsidiaries are translated using rates that approximate those effect during the period. Gains and losses from these translations are credited charged foreign currency translation included \x93accumulated other comprehensive income (loss)\x94 shareholders\x92 equity. The Company\x92 foreign manufacturing subsidiaries and certain other international subsidiaries that use the . dollar their functional currency remeasure monetary assets and liabilities exchange rates effect the end each period, and inventories, property, and nonmonetary assets and liabilities historical rates. Gains and losses from these translations were insignificant and have been included the Company\x92 results operations. Revenue Recognition Net sales consist primarily revenue from the sale hardware, software, peripherals, digital content, and service and support contracts. The Company recognizes revenue pursuant applicable accounting standards, including Statement Position (SOP) . - , Software Revenue Recognition , amended, and Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) . , Revenue Recognition . The Company recognizes revenue when persuasive evidence arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the sales price fixed determinable, and collection probable. Product considered delivered the customer once has been shipped and title and risk loss have been transferred. For most the Company\x92 product sales, these criteria are met the time the product shipped. For online sales individuals, for some sales education customers the ., and for certain other sales, the Company defers revenue until the customer receives the product because the Company legally retains portion the risk loss these sales during transit. the outset arrangement the Company determines the arrangement fee not, presumed not , fixed determinable, revenue deferred and subsequently recognized amounts become due and payable. Revenue from service and support contracts deferred and recognized ratably over the service coverage periods. These contracts typically include extended phone support, repair services, web-based support resources, diagnostic tools, and extend the service coverage offered under the Company\x92 one-year limited warranty. The Company sells software and peripheral products obtained from other companies. The Company establishes its own pricing and retains related inventory risk, the primary obligor sales transactions with its customers, and assumes the credit risk for amounts billed its customers. Accordingly, the Company recognizes revenue for the sale products obtained from other companies the gross amount billed. When the fair value delivered element has not been established, the Company uses the residual method recognize revenue the fair value all undelivered elements determinable. Under the residual method, the fair value the undelivered elements deferred and the remaining portion the arrangement fee allocated the delivered elements and recognized revenue. Note \x97Segment Information and Geographic Data accordance with SFAS . , Disclosures about Segments Enterprise and Related Information , the Company reports segment information based the \x93management\x94 approach. The management approach designates the internal reporting used management for making decisions and assessing performance the source the Company\x92 reportable segments. The Company manages its business primarily geographic basis. The Company\x92 reportable operating segments are comprised the Americas, Europe, Japan, and Retail. The Americas, Europe, and Japan reportable segments not include activities related the Retail segment. The Americas segment includes both North and South America. The Europe segment includes European countries well the Middle East and Africa. The Retail segment operates Apple-owned retail stores the ., Canada, Japan, and the . Other operating segments include Asia-Pacific, which includes Australia and Asia except for Japan, and the Company\x92 subsidiary, FileMaker, Inc. Each reportable geographic operating segment provides similar hardware and software products and similar services, and the accounting policies the various segments are the same those described Note , \x93Summary Significant Accounting Policies,\x94 except described below for the Retail segment. The Company evaluates the performance its operating segments based net sales. The Retail segment\x92 performance also evaluated based operating income. Net sales for geographic segments are generally based the location the customers. Operating income for each segment includes net sales third parties, related cost sales, and operating expenses directly attributable the segment. Operating income for each segment excludes other income and expense and certain expenses that are managed outside the operating segments. Costs excluded from segment operating income include various corporate expenses, manufacturing costs and variances not included standard costs, income taxes, and various nonrecurring charges. Corporate expenses include research and development, corporate marketing expenses, manufacturing costs and variances not included standard costs, and other separately managed general and administrative expenses including certain corporate expenses associated with support the Retail segment. The Company does not include intercompany transfers between segments for management reporting purposes. Segment assets exclude corporate assets. Corporate assets include cash, short-term and long-term investments, manufacturing facilities, miscellaneous corporate infrastructure, goodwill and other acquired intangible assets, and retail store construction- -progress that not subject depreciation. Except for the Retail segment, capital expenditures for long-lived assets are not reported management segment. Capital expenditures the Retail segment were $ million, $ million, and $ million for , , and respectively. Operating income for all segments, except Retail, includes cost sales manufacturing standard cost, other cost sales, related sales and marketing costs, and certain general and administrative costs. This measure operating income, which includes manufacturing profit, provides comparable basis for comparison between the Company\x92 various geographic segments. Certain manufacturing expenses and related adjustments not included segment cost sales, including variances between standard and actual manufacturing costs and the mark- above standard cost for product supplied the Retail segment, are included corporate expenses. Controls and Procedures Evaluation Disclosure Controls and Procedures Based evaluation under the supervision and with the participation the Company\x92 management, the Company\x92 principal executive officer and principal financial officer have concluded that the Company\x92 disclosure controls and procedures defined rules 13a- ( ) and 15d- ( ) under the Securities Exchange Act , amended (Exchange Act) were effective September , ensure that information required disclosed the Company reports that files submits under the Exchange Act ( ) recorded, processed, summarized and reported within the time periods specified the Securities and Exchange Commission rules and forms and ( ) accumulated and communicated the Company\x92 management, including its principal executive officer and principal financial officer, appropriate allow timely decisions regarding required disclosure. Inherent Limitations Over Internal Controls The Company\x92 internal control over financial reporting designed provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability financial reporting and the preparation financial statements for external purposes accordance with generally accepted accounting principles. The Company\x92 internal control over financial reporting includes those policies and procedures that: ( ) pertain the maintenance records that, reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect the transactions and dispositions the Company\x92 assets; ( ) provide reasonable assurance that transactions are recorded necessary permit preparation financial statements accordance with generally accepted accounting principles, and that the Company\x92 receipts and expenditures are being made only accordance with authorizations the Company\x92 management and directors; and (iii) provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention timely detection unauthorized acquisition, use, disposition the Company\x92 assets that could have material effect the financial statements. Management, including the Company\x92 Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer, does not expect that the Company\x92 internal controls will prevent detect all errors and all fraud. control system, matter how well designed and operated, can provide only reasonable, not absolute, assurance that the objectives the control system are met. Further, the design control system must reflect the fact that there are resource constraints, and the benefits controls must considered relative their costs. Because the inherent limitations all control systems, evaluation internal controls can provide absolute assurance that all control issues and instances fraud, any, have been detected. Also, any evaluation the effectiveness controls future periods are subject the risk that those internal controls may become inadequate because changes business conditions, that the degree compliance with the policies procedures may deteriorate. Policy Audit Committee Pre-Approval Audit and Non-Audit Services Performed the Independent Auditors Prior the enactment the Sarbanes-Oxley Act (the \x93 Act \x94), the Company adopted auditor independence policy that banned its auditors from performing non-financial consulting services, such information technology consulting and internal audit services. This auditor policy also mandates that the audit and non-audit services and related budget approved the Audit Committee advance, and that the Audit Committee provided with quarterly reporting actual spending. accordance with this policy, all services performed KPMG were pre-approved the Audit Committee. Subsequent the enactment the Act, the Audit Committee met with KPMG further understand the provisions that Act relates auditor independence. KPMG rotated the lead audit partner for fiscal year and will rotate other partners appropriate compliance with the Act. The Audit Committee will continue monitor the activities undertaken KPMG comply with the Act. Executive Overview The Company designs, manufactures, and markets personal computers and related software, services, peripherals, and networking solutions. The Company also designs, develops, and markets line portable digital music players along with related accessories and services including the online distribution third-party music, audio books, music videos, short films, and television shows. The Company\x92 products and services include the Macintosh line desktop and notebook computers, the iPod digital music player, the Xserve server and Xserve RAID storage products, portfolio consumer and professional software applications, the Mac operating system, the iTunes Music Store, portfolio peripherals that support and enhance the Macintosh and iPod product lines, and variety other service and support offerings. The Company sells its products worldwide through its online stores, its own retail stores, its direct sales force, and third-party wholesalers, resellers, and value added resellers. addition, the Company sells variety third-party Macintosh compatible products, including computer printers and printing supplies, storage devices, computer memory, digital camcorders and still cameras, personal digital assistants, and various other computing products and supplies through its online and retail stores. The Company sells education, consumer, creative professional, business, and government customers. further description the Company\x92 products may found Part , Item this document under the heading \x93Business.\x94 The Company\x92 business strategy leverages its ability, through the design and development its own operating system, hardware, and many software applications and technologies, bring its customers around the world compelling new products and solutions with superior ease- -use, seamless integration, and innovative industrial design. The Company participates several highly competitive markets, including personal computers with its Macintosh line computers, consumer electronics with its iPod line digital music players, and distribution third-party digital content through its online iTunes Music Store. While the Company widely recognized innovator the personal computer and consumer electronic markets well leader the emerging market for distribution digital content, these are all highly competitive markets that are subject aggressive pricing and increased competition. remain competitive, the Company believes that increased investment research and development ( & ) and marketing and advertising necessary maintain and extend its position the markets where competes. The Company\x92 & spending focused delivering timely updates and enhancements its existing line personal computers, displays, operating systems, software applications, and portable music players; developing new digital lifestyle consumer and professional software applications; and investing new product areas such rack-mount servers, RAID storage systems, and wireless technologies. The Company also believes investment marketing and advertising programs critical increasing product and brand awareness. June , the Company announced its plan begin using Intel microprocessors its Macintosh computers. The Company plans begin shipping certain models with Intel microprocessors June and complete the transition all its Macintosh computers Intel microprocessors the end calendar year . Allowance for Doubtful Accounts The Company distributes its products through third-party resellers and directly certain education, consumer, and commercial customers. The Company generally does not require collateral from its customers. However, when possible the Company does attempt limit credit risk trade receivables with credit insurance for certain customers Latin America, Europe, and Asia and arranging with third-party financing companies provide flooring arrangements and other loan and lease programs the Company\x92 direct customers. These credit-financing arrangements are directly between the third-party financing company and the end customer. such, the Company generally does not assume any recourse credit risk sharing related any these arrangements. However, considerable trade receivables that are not covered collateral, third-party flooring arrangements, credit insurance are outstanding with the Company\x92 distribution and retail channel partners. The allowance for doubtful accounts based management\x92 assessment the collectibility specific customer accounts and includes consideration the credit worthiness and financial condition those specific customers. The Company records allowance reduce the specific receivables the amount that reasonably believed collectible . The Company also records allowance for all other trade receivables based multiple factors including historical experience with bad debts, the general economic environment, the financial condition the Company\x92 distribution channels, and the aging such receivables. there deterioration major customer\x92 financial condition, the Company becomes aware additional information related the credit worthiness major customer, future actual default rates trade receivables general differ from those currently anticipated, the Company may have adjust its allowance for doubtful accounts, which would affect earnings the period the adjustments are made. SEQ.= ,FOLIO=' ',FILE=' :\\ \\334131149411_D11851_687824\\ - - htm',USER='jmsproofassembler', ='Nov : ' NOTES CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS Note \x97Summary Significant Accounting Policies Apple Computer, Inc. and its subsidiaries (the Company) designs, manufactures, and markets personal computers and related software, services, peripherals, and networking solutions. The Company also designs, develops, and markets line portable digital music players along with related accessories and services including the online distribution third-party music, audio books, music videos, short films, and television shows. The Company sells its products worldwide through its online stores, its own retail stores, its direct sales force, and third-party wholesalers, resellers, and value-added resellers. addition its own hardware, software, and peripheral products, the Company sells variety third-party hardware and software products through its online and retail stores. The Company sells education, consumer, creative professional, business, and government customers. Basis Presentation and Preparation The accompanying consolidated financial statements include the accounts the Company. Intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated. Financial Instruments Cash Equivalents and Short-term Investments All highly liquid investments with maturities three months less the date purchase are classified cash equivalents. Highly liquid investments with maturities greater than three months are classified short-term investments. The Company\x92 debt and marketable equity securities have been classified and accounted for available-for-sale. Management determines the appropriate classification its investments debt and marketable equity securities the time purchase and reevaluates available-for-sale designation each balance sheet date. These securities are carried fair value, with the unrealized gains and losses, net taxes, reported component shareholders\x92 equity. The cost securities sold based upon the specific identification method. Foreign Currency Translation The Company translates the assets and liabilities its international non- . functional currency subsidiaries into . dollars using exchange rates effect the end each period. Revenue and expenses for these subsidiaries are translated using rates that approximate those effect during the period. Gains and losses from these translations are credited charged foreign currency translation included \x93accumulated other comprehensive income (loss)\x94 shareholders\x92 equity. The Company\x92 foreign manufacturing subsidiaries and certain other international subsidiaries that use the . dollar their functional currency remeasure monetary assets and liabilities exchange rates effect the end each period, and inventories, property, and nonmonetary assets and liabilities historical rates. Gains and losses from these translations were insignificant and have been included the Company\x92 results operations. Revenue Recognition Net sales consist primarily revenue from the sale hardware, software, peripherals, digital content, and service and support contracts. The Company recognizes revenue pursuant applicable accounting standards, including Statement Position (SOP) . - , Software Revenue Recognition , amended, and Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) . , Revenue Recognition . The Company recognizes revenue when persuasive evidence arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the sales price fixed determinable, and collection probable. Product considered delivered the customer once has been shipped and title and risk loss have been transferred. For most the Company\x92 product sales, these criteria are met the time the product shipped. For online sales individuals, for some sales education customers the ., and for certain other sales, the Company defers revenue until the customer receives the product because the Company legally retains portion the risk loss these sales during transit. the outset arrangement the Company determines the arrangement fee not, presumed not , fixed determinable, revenue deferred and subsequently recognized amounts become due and payable. Revenue from service and support contracts deferred and recognized ratably over the service coverage periods. These contracts typically include extended phone support, repair services, web-based support resources, diagnostic tools, and extend the service coverage offered under the Company\x92 one-year limited warranty. The Company sells software and peripheral products obtained from other companies. The Company establishes its own pricing and retains related inventory risk, the primary obligor sales transactions with its customers, and assumes the credit risk for amounts billed its customers. Accordingly, the Company recognizes revenue for the sale products obtained from other companies the gross amount billed. Note \x97Segment Information and Geographic Data accordance with SFAS . , Disclosures about Segments Enterprise and Related Information , the Company reports segment information based the \x93management\x94 approach. The management approach designates the internal reporting used management for making decisions and assessing performance the source the Company\x92 reportable segments. The Company manages its business primarily geographic basis. The Company\x92 reportable operating segments are comprised the Americas, Europe, Japan, and Retail. The Americas, Europe, and Japan reportable segments not include activities related the Retail segment. The Americas segment includes both North and South America. The Europe segment includes European countries well the Middle East and Africa. The Retail segment operates Apple-owned retail stores the ., Canada, Japan, and the . Other operating segments include Asia-Pacific, which includes Australia and Asia except for Japan, and the Company\x92 subsidiary, FileMaker, Inc. Each reportable geographic operating segment provides similar hardware and software products and similar services, and the accounting policies the various segments are the same those described Note , \x93Summary Significant Accounting Policies,\x94 except described below for the Retail segment. The Company evaluates the performance its operating segments based net sales. The Retail segment\x92 performance also evaluated based operating income. Net sales for geographic segments are generally based the location the customers. Operating income for each segment includes net sales third parties, related cost sales, and operating expenses directly attributable the segment. Operating income for each segment excludes other income and expense and certain expenses that are managed outside the operating segments. Costs excluded from segment operating income include various corporate expenses, manufacturing costs and variances not included standard costs, income taxes, and various nonrecurring charges. Corporate expenses include research and development, corporate marketing expenses, manufacturing costs and variances not included standard costs, and other separately managed general and administrative expenses including certain corporate expenses associated with support the Retail segment. The Company does not include intercompany transfers between segments for management reporting purposes. Segment assets exclude corporate assets. Corporate assets include cash, short-term and long-term investments, manufacturing facilities, miscellaneous corporate infrastructure, goodwill and other acquired intangible assets, and retail store construction- -progress that not subject depreciation. Except for the Retail segment, capital expenditures for long-lived assets are not reported management segment. Capital expenditures the Retail segment were $ million, $ million, and $ million for , , and respectively. Operating income for all segments, except Retail, includes cost sales manufacturing standard cost, other cost sales, related sales and marketing costs, and certain general and administrative costs. This measure operating income, which includes manufacturing profit, provides comparable basis for comparison between the Company\x92 various geographic segments. Certain manufacturing expenses and related adjustments not included segment cost sales, including variances between standard and actual manufacturing costs and the mark- above standard cost for product supplied the Retail segment, are included corporate expenses. The Company\x92 internal control over financial reporting includes those policies and procedures that: ( ) pertain the maintenance records that, reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect the transactions and dispositions the Company\x92 assets; ( ) provide reasonable assurance that transactions are recorded necessary permit preparation financial statements accordance with generally accepted accounting principles, and that the Company\x92 receipts and expenditures are being made only accordance with authorizations the Company\x92 management and directors; and (iii) provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention timely detection unauthorized acquisition, use, disposition the Company\x92 assets that could have material effect the financial statements. Because the inherent limitations all control systems, evaluation internal controls can provide absolute assurance that all control issues and instances fraud, any, have been detected. Policy Audit Committee Pre-Approval Audit and Non-Audit Services Performed the Independent Auditors Prior the enactment the Sarbanes-Oxley Act (the \x93 Act \x94), the Company adopted auditor independence policy that banned its auditors from performing non-financial consulting services, such information technology consulting and internal audit services. This auditor policy also mandates that the audit and non-audit services and related budget approved the Audit Committee advance, and that the Audit Committee provided with quarterly reporting actual spending. accordance with this policy, all services performed KPMG were pre-approved the Audit Committee. Subsequent the enactment the Act, the Audit Committee met with KPMG further understand the provisions that Act relates auditor independence. KPMG rotated the lead audit partner for fiscal year and will rotate other partners appropriate compliance with the Act. The Audit Committee will continue monitor the activities undertaken KPMG comply with the Act.
